  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_6cbd641a-63ba-4b84-a419-9271a140ae08'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4285031804686856136">إنّه زمن “القوقعة”، حيث يختلط كل شيء. لا حدود فاصلة بين الماضي والحاضر، السوريالي والواقعي. هي ليست مجرّد رواية يقصّها علينا أحدهم. هي نص يختزن الرعب، الخوف، الظلم..الإحتضار. تدور الأحداث في ثمانينيّات القرن الماضي، أثناء احتدام الصراع المسلّح بين النظام السوري والأخوان المسلمين. يعود “مصطفى خليفة” إلى بلاده من فرنسا، بعد حصوله على إجازة في الإخراج السينمائي. “بلادي (سوريا</span>
  <span id="freeText4285031804686856136" style="display:none">إنّه زمن “القوقعة”، حيث يختلط كل شيء. لا حدود فاصلة بين الماضي والحاضر، السوريالي والواقعي. هي ليست مجرّد رواية يقصّها علينا أحدهم. هي نص يختزن الرعب، الخوف، الظلم..الإحتضار. تدور الأحداث في ثمانينيّات القرن الماضي، أثناء احتدام الصراع المسلّح بين النظام السوري والأخوان المسلمين. يعود “مصطفى خليفة” إلى بلاده من فرنسا، بعد حصوله على إجازة في الإخراج السينمائي. “بلادي (سوريا) بحاجة إليّ أكثر من أي دولة أُخْرَى”. وهكذا كان. يترك مصطفى خلفه كل شيء: صديقته، مقاهي باريس، حقوق الإنسان، البيرة، وأشياء أُخْرَى.. يصل إلى المطار. يوقفه الأمن السوري. يأخذوه إلى التحقيق، بتهمة الانتماء إلى تنظيم “الإخوان المسلمين”، علماً انه مسيحي حسب الهويّة، وملحد في المعتقد. وهناك، يختفي مصطفى لمدّة 13 سنة، ثلاثة أشهر وثلاثة عشرة يوماً، في سجون النظام.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4285031804686856136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34329421-the-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2404765795" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6329332738695566064">This is a terrifying and heartbreaking (and, apparently, realistic) portrayal of life inside Assad's prisons. The protagonist is a Syrian christian from a communist family who gets sent to the infamous regime prison in palmyra for more than a decade, suffers unimaginable abuse, and somehow survives. It is based on the author's own experiences. If you want to understand the true nature of the Assad regime you should read this book.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2450967173" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2450967173" />
    <a title="Yaman" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68316449-yaman"><img alt="Yaman" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541545763p2/68316449.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2450967173?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Yaman" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Yaman" href="/user/show/68316449-yaman">Yaman</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2450967173" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1315642382628284861"><br/>Writing this review in English as I hope that sharing it might make you want to pick up the translated version – audiences in the non-Arab World are unfamiliar with the dense issue that is being discussed here. I’d say not even most Arabs are aware of its extent. <br/><br/>It has been a very long while since I found a book compelling enough for me to read it in one sitting. "The Shell: Memoirs of a Hidden Observer" is... unbelievable, to say the least. It’s definitely one of the most, if not the most, pow</span>
  <span id="freeText1315642382628284861" style="display:none"><br />Writing this review in English as I hope that sharing it might make you want to pick up the translated version – audiences in the non-Arab World are unfamiliar with the dense issue that is being discussed here. I’d say not even most Arabs are aware of its extent. <br /><br />It has been a very long while since I found a book compelling enough for me to read it in one sitting. "The Shell: Memoirs of a Hidden Observer" is... unbelievable, to say the least. It’s definitely one of the most, if not the most, powerful and courageous works I’ve ever put my hands on. <br /><br />A Catholic man from Syria returns home after studying in France, only to be picked up at the airport by Syrian intelligence. He’s then sent to spend the next decade of his life in a military prison – Palmyra Military Prison, as implied by context. All part of the insanity that drove Assad (the father) to turn the entire country into one large prison in the 1980s.<br /><br />Prisons under both Assads, in general, have long been considered hell on earth, matched in barbarity by none other than North Korea. They’ve been documented as inhumane slaughterhouses by human rights agencies, and while reading this book I could only remember Amnesty International’s detailed report and pictures exposing one of these torture chambers. <br /><br />This book is talking exactly about that. It’s a shocking account on the ugly, revolting nature of these prisons. I can’t find the proper words to describe the level of dehumanization imposed on prisoners of conscience in Syria, but this book does. Its pages show the reader the sickening sadism committed on arbitrary basis in these prisons to subjugate Syrians and humiliate them into becoming slaves to the regime and its militias. <br /><br />Reading this book might make you feel nauseous, but that’s exactly the point: it’s an honest description of life in Assad’s Syria. Definitely a must-read for anyone interested in Syria’s past and why it lead to Syria of the present. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="1315642382628284861" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/377263651" />
    <a title="Noha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4842213-noha"><img alt="Noha" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/377263651?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2012</a>

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4842213-noha?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4842213-noha?shelf=smooth-flow">smooth-flow</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4842213-noha?shelf=must-be-read-at-least-once">must-be-read-at-least-once</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer377263651" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10814733476939332235">Despite the fact that the book is so depressing (for all the injustice mentioned in the book), it takes the reader deeply in the world of the book. It touches your heart.<br/><br/>The prisoners were unbelievably idealistic to me (compared to the characters in Sharaf by the author Sonalla Ibrahim). They were very righteous, logical, and selfless; characteristics that would disappear in such an ordeal. For the prison keepers, I still don't get how they turn into such sadistic creatures! The author did expla</span>
  <span id="freeText10814733476939332235" style="display:none">Despite the fact that the book is so depressing (for all the injustice mentioned in the book), it takes the reader deeply in the world of the book. It touches your heart.<br /><br />The prisoners were unbelievably idealistic to me (compared to the characters in Sharaf by the author Sonalla Ibrahim). They were very righteous, logical, and selfless; characteristics that would disappear in such an ordeal. For the prison keepers, I still don't get how they turn into such sadistic creatures! The author did explain the turn briefly but still... <br /><br />I liked the fact that the author did not specify a country (even though it was obvious what country it was, from the dialogue); the torturing for political cases happens in every Arab country. <br /><br />The thing about reading prison literature is that one sees and appreciates the little things in his life; the little things that are the basic of freedom. <br /><br />ربنا يفك أسر كل المحبوسين ظلما </span>
  <a data-text-id="10814733476939332235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2186090567" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2186090567" />
    <a title="Corey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8386063-corey"><img alt="Corey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528466470p2/8386063.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2186090567?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corey" href="/user/show/8386063-corey">Corey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781566560221" href="/book/show/30961992-the-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8386063-corey?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2186090567" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8749939862966066414">A book that is at one and the same time incredibly important and completely unreadable. I made it about halfway through before giving up. It's a Syrian prison memoir, but there's no plot, and very little reflection--just page after page of description of what hell on Earth is truly like. If you can make it through this, you're a better person than I.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a title="Peter King" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Peter King" href="/user/show/14042714-peter-king">Peter King</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34329421-the-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255456025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7537617063046224285">This book doesn't read like a normal novel - more like an autobiography. It's the story of a Syrian who finds himself imprisoned by the Assad regime for being Muslim Brotherhood, although he's actually a Christian and the Syrian authorities neither know nor care why he's in prison. <br/>Frankly, it's a tough read. I thought reading about Treblinka was tough. This was on a par. It's awful. It's basically a story of mental survival. Living, crammed closely with people who mistrust, despise and hate you</span>
  <span id="freeText7537617063046224285" style="display:none">This book doesn't read like a normal novel - more like an autobiography. It's the story of a Syrian who finds himself imprisoned by the Assad regime for being Muslim Brotherhood, although he's actually a Christian and the Syrian authorities neither know nor care why he's in prison. <br />Frankly, it's a tough read. I thought reading about Treblinka was tough. This was on a par. It's awful. It's basically a story of mental survival. Living, crammed closely with people who mistrust, despise and hate you while your guards casually torture you (500 lashes on the feet is the standard punishment for opening your eyes in the exercise yard) and execute people randomly around you. <br />Mustafa Khalifa's depiction is not drawn entirely from his own 12 year stint in Tadmur prison but is an amalgam of experiences of others. It is about the damage done to human beings by terror and personality cults and makes clear that Assad is fundamentally no different to Saddam Hussein or any other post-war Middle East CIA creation.This is not a Disney story. There is no happy ending, there is only a kind of numb relief. <br />If you feel slightly sorry for yourself, this book is the antidote. If you are interested in Syria and the Middle East, this book is essential to understand the evil of the Assad regime. But fun or enjoyable, it is not.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7537617063046224285" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1575405377" />
    <a title="Moez Lamti" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13583336-moez-lamti"><img alt="Moez Lamti" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1558849018p2/13583336.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1575405377?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Moez Lamti" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Moez Lamti" href="/user/show/13583336-moez-lamti">Moez Lamti</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1575405377" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer492316287416679991">Notwithstanding the terror of real events which the story is a pale representation of, this book is quite weak. And except for some occasional lyrical escapades here and there, the best being centred around the symbolism of the titular shell itself, everything else is a lifeless description of the mundane life of a Christian captive in Syrian prisons sometime in the early eighties. There is bitter irony and a lot of insignificance in the situation, but the writer lacked the skill to turn it into</span>
  <span id="freeText492316287416679991" style="display:none">Notwithstanding the terror of real events which the story is a pale representation of, this book is quite weak. And except for some occasional lyrical escapades here and there, the best being centred around the symbolism of the titular shell itself, everything else is a lifeless description of the mundane life of a Christian captive in Syrian prisons sometime in the early eighties. There is bitter irony and a lot of insignificance in the situation, but the writer lacked the skill to turn it into art. . It's clear the writer has given up any effort to find meaning around him, and why wouldn't he, given the absurdity of what befell him, but that's so damn depressing that any reader would like to see an inkling of light even if it flaunts the precepts of reality. An interesting part of the narrative relates to Muslim brothers, who were portrayed with candid admiration; they seemed to possess what he lacked: calm and matter-of-fact reaction to imminent death. Yet for obvious ideological reasons, the writer could never part of that group, or part of any other community either. It's a story of a kafkaesque entity with blunted instincts and no hope of redemption who wonders why doesn't he die.</span>
  <a data-text-id="492316287416679991" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9894270484637493353">How do you review and rate someone's torture and prison story? "5 stars, great torture methods, very emotional, would recommend"? Or the opposite "horrible to read about, makes me vomit - one star"? This "inspired by real life but apparently not meant as non-fiction" account of life in a Syrian prison is hard to read about. It is gut-wrenchingly brutal and unfair, dehumanizing and horrible. Maybe a very important book right now, as a realization for all those idiots out there that think Syrians </span>
  <span id="freeText9894270484637493353" style="display:none">How do you review and rate someone's torture and prison story? "5 stars, great torture methods, very emotional, would recommend"? Or the opposite "horrible to read about, makes me vomit - one star"? This "inspired by real life but apparently not meant as non-fiction" account of life in a Syrian prison is hard to read about. It is gut-wrenchingly brutal and unfair, dehumanizing and horrible. Maybe a very important book right now, as a realization for all those idiots out there that think Syrians flee to Europe to steal our jobs. No, they flee because they have experienced something like this or fear experiencing it. So even though it will make you vomit up your dinner at times, and definitely makes you thankful for the safety and justice-system we have, this is a book I can recommend everyone to read. In terms of a review, I would have liked a bit more background information about the different religious and political groups to better understand some of the conflict between different factions of prisoners. And a focus on the life after prison, at least a little more. The coping, the memories, the solutions - that was done, but a bit too short for my taste. </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer4099172675463974233">I personally thought that The Shell was a very interesting memoir that gives readers a perspective into Syrian prisons. Mustafa Khalifa leaves Paris to return to his home country of Syria. However, he is not greeted with open arms as he is immediately detained and imprisoned. This is due to the fact that someone in Paris wrote a letter to the current regime stating that Mustafa said something against them. He is transferred from prison to prison as he is tortured by guards to reveal what group h</span>
  <span id="freeText4099172675463974233" style="display:none">I personally thought that The Shell was a very interesting memoir that gives readers a perspective into Syrian prisons. Mustafa Khalifa leaves Paris to return to his home country of Syria. However, he is not greeted with open arms as he is immediately detained and imprisoned. This is due to the fact that someone in Paris wrote a letter to the current regime stating that Mustafa said something against them. He is transferred from prison to prison as he is tortured by guards to reveal what group he belongs to. I thought the book was fascinating because of the author's unique situation and the fact that the author lived to tell the story. I would recommend this book to a friend if they were interested in memoirs or life in other countries. </span>

<div id="review_2826801175" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<div id="review_2570203714" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2570203714" />
    <a title="Edward Etzkorn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/37377669-edward-etzkorn"><img alt="Edward Etzkorn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1541281177p2/37377669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2570203714?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Edward Etzkorn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Edward Etzkorn" href="/user/show/37377669-edward-etzkorn">Edward Etzkorn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781566560221" href="/book/show/30961992-the-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/37377669-edward-etzkorn?shelf=general-fiction">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2570203714" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6597854042979480138">This book probes depths of the suffering one person can impose on another, and the strength of will required to survive it. The protagonist is a Syrian political prisoner arrested in error and the tortures to which he is subjected over the next 13 years. Written in the first-person, it makes the events feel more alive and more personal. Although it is said to be a novel, the descriptions, both of external events as well as internal psychological suffering, feel too real to be fictional.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2129196644" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2129196644" />
    <a title="R" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/61580103-r"><img alt="R" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555202136p2/61580103.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2129196644?book_show_action=true">Sep 19, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="R" class="user" itemprop="url" name="R" href="/user/show/61580103-r">R</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/34329421-the-shell">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2129196644" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11681326852409961712">I am a bit late on writing a review for this book, but it's due to the sheer fact that I had no idea what to say or where to begin. This book swallowed me up, heart and soul and it is one of my favorite books that I have read in 2017. Trying to find the right words to describe my feelings for it was like trying trying to describe what dark energy really means. It was tough, kinda confusing and mentally exhausting. BUT, I figured I'd give it my best and try to encourage everyone and anyone to rea</span>
  <span id="freeText11681326852409961712" style="display:none">I am a bit late on writing a review for this book, but it's due to the sheer fact that I had no idea what to say or where to begin. This book swallowed me up, heart and soul and it is one of my favorite books that I have read in 2017. Trying to find the right words to describe my feelings for it was like trying trying to describe what dark energy really means. It was tough, kinda confusing and mentally exhausting. BUT, I figured I'd give it my best and try to encourage everyone and anyone to read this book. <br /><br />The story takes form of a diary written by Khalifa, an atheist mistaken for a radical Islamist after returning to Syria. What makes this story so fascinating is how the diary is written. Mustafa kept the words of the diary locked away in his head day in and day out and had them written down in diary form upon his release from Tadmor. Mustafa was locked away in Tadmor, one of the most notorious prisons in the Middle East for 13 years without ever being granted a fair trial. Anytime the author described the prison and the inmates around him, you could feel the isolation and violence of it all through his writing. Mustafa delivers a detailed look of the atrocities the Assad regime is capable of doing, yet all the while, providing a critical standpoint on the tragedy the Syrian people are living through. <br /><br />Mustafa's story will capture every ounce of your attention from the beginning right until the very end. It's a tough, brutal, heartbreaking read, but it's an extremely important one. It's a book worth having on your shelf and I would certainly recommend it to anyone a million times over:) </span>
  <a data-text-id="11681326852409961712" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UwwOdTr/WGuspE2ARNQHe8TiKokgffZlXq93AtAW+vtMNZDrzjw6an0xusw/CmN4Q2fnQDcv6idx7FELAEZcxA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8ag80jNUEG3SjwjN7jo+rUbxA+dDaS9GdbZCUnrPA0vukaJMx5dybAMa/4GV5FquwXTOLlQ7MwRa9WRbqp+ldA==')})
  }

Born in 1953, Malika Oufkir was the eldest daughter of General Oufkir, the King of Morocco\'s closest aide. Adopted by the king at the age of five, Malika spent most of her childhood and adolescence in the seclusion of the court harem, one of the most eligible heiresses in the kingdom, surrounded by luxury and extraordinary privilege. Then, on August 16, 1972, her father was arrested and executed after an attempt to assassinate the king. Malika, her five younger brothers and sisters. and her mother were immediately imprisoned in a desert penal colony. After fifteen years, the last ten of which they spent locked up in solitary cells, the Oufkir children managed to dig a tunnel with their bare hands and make an audacious escape. Recaptured after five days, Malika was finally able to leave Morocco and begin a new life in exile in 1996. نقرأ مناجاة هيبا لربه &quot;\n-- د. جابر عصفور\n\n&quot;يوسف زيدان هو أول روائي مسلم، يكتب عن اللاهوت المسيحي بشكل روائي عميق. وهو أول مسلم، يحاول أن يعطي حلولا لمشكلات كنسية كبرى.. إن يوسف زيدان اقتحم حياة الأديرة، ورسم بريشة راهب أحداثا كنسية حدثت بالفعل، وكان لها أثر عظيم في تاريخ الكنيسة القبطية&quot;\n-- المطران يوحنا جريجووريوس<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"1424126319422013747\" <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4688388387858109992">مصطفى خليفة كاتب سوري ، درس الإخراج والفن في فرنسا، ليس لديه أية توجهات سياسية وتوجهاته كانت فنية بحتة، أمضى ثلاث عشرة سنة في السجن بتهمة الانتماء لجماعة الإخوان المسلمين التي واجهت النظام في ثمانينيات القرن الماضي، وهو صاحب رواية القوقعة.<br/>تم اعتقاله في مطار دمشق في الثمانينات لدى عودته من باريس، حيث كان عازماً وشاحذاً همته على المشاركة في بناء وطنه والعيش في كنفه، إلا أن يد الأجهزة الأمنية طالته ب</span>
  <span id="freeText4688388387858109992" style="display:none">مصطفى خليفة كاتب سوري ، درس الإخراج والفن في فرنسا، ليس لديه أية توجهات سياسية وتوجهاته كانت فنية بحتة، أمضى ثلاث عشرة سنة في السجن بتهمة الانتماء لجماعة الإخوان المسلمين التي واجهت النظام في ثمانينيات القرن الماضي، وهو صاحب رواية القوقعة.<br />تم اعتقاله في مطار دمشق في الثمانينات لدى عودته من باريس، حيث كان عازماً وشاحذاً همته على المشاركة في بناء وطنه والعيش في كنفه، إلا أن يد الأجهزة الأمنية طالته بسبب تقرير دُس فيه، وذكر فيه وقائع إحدى السهرات الباريسية والتي كان مصطفى خليفة أقحم في إحدى نقاشاتها السياسية ليدلو بدلوه ويتفوه بنكة سياسية تطال الرئيس الراحل وقتها حافظ الأسد الذي كان في أوج صراعه الشرس على التشبث في حكم سوريا.<br />هذا التقرير حكم على مصطفى خليفة مرهف الحس بالسجن في أعتى سجون العالم قسوة ثلاثة عشر عاماً، ذاق خلالها أنكى أنواع التنكيل والعذاب النفسي والجسدي والجنسي بسبب تقرير من زميل في فرنسا، وبسبب عدم اكتراث أي جهاز أمني في إعطائه أية قيمة للنظر في أمره أو السماح له بشرح موضوعه والتكلم إليهم.<br /><br />خرج من السجن في أواخر التسعينيات لينصدم بالمجتمع في الخارج وليكون خرج من سجن صغير إلى سجن كبير. صدم بشدة عند خروجه من السجن بوفاة والديه اللذين كانا ينتظرانه في المطار قبل ثلاثة عشر سنة ولكنه لم يصل.<br /></span>
